## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: thermomechanical constitutive modeling (materials science)
**Analysis**: This task seeks a constitutive relationship between stress, strain, and temperature. In materials science, stress typically increases with strain through elastic or hardening behavior, while temperature causes thermal softening, often through exponential or power-law mechanisms.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's law (temperature-dependent): sigma = c0 * epsilon * (c1 + c2 * T) (linear elasticity with temperature-dependent modulus)
- Linear thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (1 + c1 * T) (elastic modulus linearly dependent on temperature)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (strain hardening without temperature dependence)
- Power-law with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (1 + c2 * T)**c3 (combined hardening and softening)
- Johnson-Cook type model: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 + c3 * T) (strain hardening with linear thermal term)
- Exponential thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (Arrhenius-type temperature dependence)
- Voce hardening with temperature: sigma = (c0 + c1 * (1 - exp(c2 * epsilon))) * exp(c3 * T) (saturation hardening with thermal softening)
- Ramberg-Osgood inverse form: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2 (elastic plus plastic strain hardening)
- Hollomon with temperature: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * T**c2 (power-law in both strain and temperature)
- Ludwik model: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (yield stress plus power-law hardening)
- Arrhenius-type constitutive: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * (c3 * T)) (thermally activated deformation)
- Polynomial with cross-term: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * T + c2 * epsilon * T (bilinear interaction model)
- Sinh-based model: sigma = c0 * sinh(c1 * epsilon) * exp(c2 * T) (hyperbolic sine creep-type law)
- Rational temperature softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (c2 * T + c3)**c4 (generalized thermal factor)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Strain hardening saturation → Use (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) to capture stress saturation at large strains (Voce-type behavior)
- Thermal softening of elastic modulus → Multiply strain term by a decreasing function of T, such as (c0 - c1*T) or exp(-c*T)
- Yield stress offset → Additive constant c0 in stress expression represents initial yield strength independent of strain
- Thermally activated flow → Arrhenius factor exp(c/T) or exp(-c*T) indicates dislocation motion governed by thermal activation energy
- Strain-temperature coupling → Product terms epsilon*T or epsilon**c1 * T**c2 capture interaction between mechanical and thermal effects
- Power-law universality in plasticity → epsilon**c with 0 < c < 1 is nearly universal for work hardening in metals
- Homologous temperature scaling → Temperature often appears as (T - c0) or (c0*T) representing distance from a reference or melting temperature
- Concave-up vs concave-down strain response → Power exponent c < 1 gives concave-down (hardening saturation), c > 1 gives concave-up (accelerating hardening)

Wait, let me reconsider. `log(epsilon+1)` can be written differently. And `T*log(epsilon+1)` — many candidates have `epsilon*log(epsilon+1)` instead of `log(epsilon+1)`. These are different basis functions.

Let me re-examine the GT more carefully:

GT = `c0*epsilon**3 - c2*(T-c3) + c4*(T-c5)*log(epsilon+c6)`

Since c3 = c5 = 289.08..., this simplifies to:
GT = `c0*epsilon**3 + (T - 289.08)*(-c2 + c4*log(epsilon+1))`
= `c0*epsilon**3 - c2*T + c2*289.08 + c4*T*log(epsilon+1) - c4*289.08*log(epsilon+1)`

Basis functions: {`epsilon**3`, `T`, `1`, `T*log(epsilon+1)`, `log(epsilon+1)`}

Now let me check each candidate systematically. I'll focus on whether each candidate can produce exactly these basis functions.

**Candidates with `epsilon*log(...+1)` instead of `log(...+1)` and `T*log(...+1)`:** These cannot match because `epsilon*log(epsilon+1)` is linearly independent from `log(epsilon+1)` and `T*log(epsilon+1)`.

**Candidates with `T*epsilon` terms:** The GT has no `T*epsilon` term (it has `T*log(epsilon+1)`). If a candidate has `T*c1*epsilon`, this can only be zeroed out (c1=0), but then we lose the ability to generate `T*log(epsilon+1)`.

Let me now go through each candidate:

### Candidate 1:
`T*c0 + T*c1*epsilon + c2 + c3*epsilon + c4*epsilon**4 + c5*sin(c6*epsilon + c7) + c8*epsilon*log(c9*epsilon + 1)`

Basis functions available: {T, T*epsilon, 1, epsilon, epsilon**4, sin(c6*epsilon+c7), epsilon*log(c9*epsilon+1)}

GT needs `T*log(epsilon+1)` — not available. Has `T*epsilon` instead. Cannot match.
Also has `epsilon**4` instead of `epsilon**3`, and `epsilon*log(...)` instead of `log(...)`.

Candidate 1 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 2:
`T*c0 + T*c1*epsilon + c2 + c3*epsilon**4 + c4*sin(c5*epsilon + c6) + c7*epsilon*log(c8*epsilon + 1)`

Similar issues: has `T*epsilon` but not `T*log(epsilon+1)`, has `epsilon**4` not `epsilon**3`.

Candidate 2 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 3:

Has `epsilon**3*exp(T*c8)` — if c8=0, this becomes `epsilon**3`, giving us that basis function. But then we need `T*log(epsilon+1)` which isn't available. Has `T*epsilon**4` but not `T*log(epsilon+1)`.
